# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-benchmarks/flipt--3d5a345f`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-benchmarks/flipt--3d5a345f$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-benchmarks/flipt--3d5a345f` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Generate Flipt Release Notes

**Repository:** github.com/sg-benchmarks/flipt--3d5a345f (mirror of flipt-io/flipt)
**Output:** Write your release notes to `/workspace/RELEASE_NOTES.md`

## Objective

Generate comprehensive release notes for Flipt summarizing API changes. Flipt is an open-source feature flag management system with REST and gRPC APIs. Analyze the codebase to identify what changed in terms of the public API surface.

## Scope

Analyze the following areas for API changes:
- `rpc/flipt/` — protobuf API definitions (gRPC surface)
- `internal/server/` — REST API handlers
- `internal/storage/` — storage backend changes
- `ui/` — frontend changes if any significant ones exist
- `CHANGELOG.md` in the repository (use as reference, not as copy)

## Output Format

Write to `/workspace/RELEASE_NOTES.md`:

```markdown
# Flipt Release Notes

## Breaking Changes

> These changes require action from users upgrading.

- **[API/Storage/Config]**: Description + migration path

## New Features

- **[component]**: Description with API example if applicable

## Deprecations

- **[component]**: What is deprecated, what to use instead, when it will be removed

## Bug Fixes

- **[component]**: Description

## Upgrade Guide

Step-by-step instructions for users upgrading from the previous version.
```

## Quality Bar

- Every breaking change must include a migration path
- Every deprecation must specify the replacement
- New features must reference the specific API endpoint or config option
- The upgrade guide must be actionable (numbered steps)

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not copy the existing CHANGELOG.md
- Do not fabricate API endpoints — verify in rpc/ or internal/server/

     2→
     3→## Overview
     4→
     5→These release notes document the API and configuration changes in Flipt since v1.40.1, including new features, improvements, and important information for upgrading.
     6→
     7→## Breaking Changes
     8→
     9→No breaking changes identified in this release. All API changes are backward compatible.
    10→
    11→## New Features
    12→
    13→### Configuration: Remote Blob Storage Support
    14→
    15→**Added in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)
    16→
    17→Flipt now supports loading configuration files from remote blob storage backends. This enables storing your Flipt configuration in cloud object storage (S3, Azure Blob Storage, Google Cloud Storage) instead of local filesystem.
    18→
    19→#### Supported Schemes
    20→- **S3:** `s3://bucket-name/path/to/config.yml`
    21→- **Azure Blob Storage:** `azblob://container/path/to/config.yml`
    22→- **Google Cloud Storage:** `gs://bucket-name/path/to/config.yml`
    23→
    24→#### Configuration Example
    25→```bash
    26→# Load configuration from S3
    27→FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=s3://my-bucket/flipt-config.yml
    28→
    29→# Load configuration from Azure Blob Storage
    30→FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=azblob://mycontainer/flipt-config.yml
    31→
    32→# Load configuration from Google Cloud Storage
    33→FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=gs://my-bucket/flipt-config.yml
    34→```
    35→
    36→#### API Details
    37→- Configuration is loaded via the `getConfigFile()` function in `internal/config/config.go`
    38→- The function supports URLs with schemes mapped to object storage backends
    39→- Falls back to local filesystem if no recognized remote scheme is detected
    40→- Requires appropriate cloud provider credentials/authentication configured in your en

Excellent! I've successfully generated comprehensive release notes for Flipt at `/workspace/RELEASE_NOTES.md`. Here's a summary of what I documented:

## Release Notes Summary

### **Breaking Changes**
✅ None identified - all changes are backward compatible

### **New Features**

1. **Remote Blob Storage Support for Configuration** (after v1.40.1)
   - Load configuration from S3, Azure Blob Storage, or Google Cloud Storage
   - Supports URLs like `s3://bucket/config.yml`, `azblob://container/config.yml`, `gs://bucket/config.yml`
   - Implementation via `getConfigFile()` in `internal/config/config.go`

2. **OpenTelemetry Tracing: Sampling Ratio** (after v1.40.1)
   - New `samplingRatio` config parameter (0.0-1.0)
   - Reduces trace overhead in production environments
   - Applied at TracerProvider level using OpenTelemetry SDK's `TraceIDRatioBased` sampler

3. **Analytics: Entity ID Tracking** (after v1.40.1)
   - Entity ID now captured in ClickHouse analytics
   - Enables better insights into entity usage patterns

### **Improvements**

- **Auth Database Optimization** - Skip unnecessary database connections
- **Auth Cache Optimization** - Store only hashes, not full auth data
- **Enhanced OpenTelemetry Resources** - Includes service version, container info, process runtime details (semantic conventions v1.24.0)

### **Deprecations**

1. **Jaeger Tracing** (since v1.36.0) → Use OTLP instead
2. **List API Offset Parameter** (since v1.13.0) → Use `page_token` instead

### **Documentation Included**

✅ Configuration examples (YAML and environment variables)
✅ API details and protobuf structure changes  
✅ Migration paths for all deprecations
✅ Step-by-step upgrade guide
✅ Storage backend support matrix
✅ Performance recommendations
✅ Rollback procedures

The release notes

  "content": "# Flipt Release Notes\n\n## Overview\n\nThese release notes document the API and configuration changes in Flipt since v1.40.1, including new features, improvements, and important information for upgrading.\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\nNo breaking changes identified in this release. All API changes are backward compatible.\n\n## New Features\n\n### Configuration: Remote Blob Storage Support\n\n**Added in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)\n\nFlipt now supports loading configuration files from remote blob storage backends. This enables storing your Flipt configuration in cloud object storage (S3, Azure Blob Storage, Google Cloud Storage) instead of local filesystem.\n\n#### Supported Schemes\n- **S3:** `s3://bucket-name/path/to/config.yml`\n- **Azure Blob Storage:** `azblob://container/path/to/config.yml`\n- **Google Cloud Storage:** `gs://bucket-name/path/to/config.yml`\n\n#### Configuration Example\n```bash\n# Load configuration from S3\nFLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=s3://my-bucket/flipt-config.yml\n\n# Load configuration from Azure Blob Storage\nFLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=azblob://mycontainer/flipt-config.yml\n\n# Load configuration from Google Cloud Storage\nFLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=gs://my-bucket/flipt-config.yml\n```\n\n#### API Details\n- Configuration is loaded via the `getConfigFile()` function in `internal/config/config.go`\n- The function supports URLs with schemes mapped to object storage backends\n- Falls back to local filesystem if no recognized remote scheme is detected\n- Requires appropriate cloud provider credentials/authentication configured in your environment\n\n#### Migration Path\nNo migration needed. This is a new optional feature. You can continue using local configuration paths or migrate by:\n1. Upload your current `flipt.yml` to your cloud storage\n2. Set `FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH` environment variable to the remote URL\n3. Restart Flipt\n\n---\n\n### Tracing: Sampling Ratio Configuration\n\n**Added in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)\n\nEnhanced OpenTelemetry tracing instrumentation with configurable trace sampling ratio. This allows you to control the percentage of requests that generate traces, reducing overhead in high-traffic environments.\n\n#### Configuration Schema\n\n**YAML Configuration:**\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: otlp\n  samplingRatio: 0.1  # Sample 10% of traces\n  otlp:\n    endpoint: http://localhost:4317\n```\n\n**Environment Variable:**\n```bash\nFLIPT_TRACING_SAMPLINGRATIO=0.1\n```\n\n#### Valid Values\n- Minimum: `0` (no traces sampled)\n- Maximum: `1` (all traces sampled, default)\n- Recommended for production: `0.1` to `0.5`\n\n#### Configuration Details\n- **Type:** Float64 (0.0 - 1.0)\n- **Default:** `1` (sample all traces)\n- **Validation:** Flipt validates that the value is between 0 and 1 at startup\n\n#### Implementation\n- Implemented using OpenTelemetry SDK's `TraceIDRatioBased` sampler\n- Applied at the TracerProvider level in `internal/tracing/tracing.go`\n- Sampler is initialized with: `tracesdk.TraceIDRatioBased(cfg.SamplingRatio)`\n\n#### API Example\nWhen creating a tracer provider programmatically:\n```go\ncfg := config.TracingConfig{\n    Enabled: true,\n    Exporter: config.TracingOTLP,\n    SamplingRatio: 0.1,\n}\nprovider, err := tracing.NewProvider(ctx, version, cfg)\n```\n\n#### Migration Path\n- This is a new optional feature; no migration required\n- Default behavior (sample all traces) unchanged unless explicitly configured\n- To reduce sampling:\n  1. Update your configuration file or environment variable\n  2. Set `samplingRatio` to desired value (e.g., `0.1` for 10%)\n  3. Restart Flipt\n\n---\n\n### Analytics: Entity ID Tracking\n\n**Added in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)\n\nEntity ID is now tracked in analytics data when using ClickHouse as the analytics backend. This enables better insights into which entities are being evaluated.\n\n#### Details\n- Entity ID values are now captured and stored in the analytics event stream\n- Tracked in addition to existing metrics (flag key, namespace, etc.)\n- Applies to ClickHouse analytics backend\n- Analytics can be queried to analyze entity usage patterns\n\n#### Configuration\nNo new configuration required. If you have ClickHouse analytics enabled, entity ID tracking is automatic:\n\n```yaml\nanalytics:\n  storage:\n    type: clickhouse\n    clickhouse:\n      endpoint: http://localhost:8123\n```\n\n---\n\n## Improvements\n\n### Authentication: Database Connection Optimization\n\n**Fixed in:** v1.40.1 (includes auth improvements)\n\nAuthentication backend now avoids establishing unnecessary database connections:\n- Connections are only established when authentication methods require them\n- Reduces database connection pool overhead\n- Improves startup time for authentication configurations that don't need a database\n\n#### Details\n- Applied in `internal/server/authn/` module\n- Only methods like token authentication that require database access will establish connections\n- Methods like OAuth/OIDC that don't need database remain lightweight\n\n---\n\n### Authentication: Cache Optimization\n\n**Fixed in:** v1.40.1\n\nAuthentication hash caching now stores only the hash rather than full authentication data:\n- Reduces cache memory usage\n- Improves cache performance\n- More secure (hashes instead of full auth data in cache)\n\n#### Implementation\n- Cache middleware in `internal/server/middleware/`\n- Only authentication hash is cached (`auth.Hash`)\n- Full authentication data still retrieved as needed\n\n---\n\n### OpenTelemetry Resource Attributes\n\n**Improved in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)\n\nOpenTelemetry tracing now includes enhanced resource information:\n- Service name: `flipt`\n- Service version: Current Flipt version\n- OTEL environment variables: Automatically detected from environment\n- Telemetry SDK information: Included in traces\n- Container information: Detected if running in container\n- Host information: System hostname/IP included\n- Process runtime details: Go version and runtime information\n\n#### Details\n- Implements OpenTelemetry semantic conventions v1.24.0\n- Applied when creating trace resource in `internal/tracing/tracing.go`\n- Configured in `newResource()` function with:\n  - `resource.WithFromEnv()` - picks up OTEL_* environment variables\n  - `resource.WithTelemetrySDK()` - includes SDK version\n  - `resource.WithContainer()` - container detection\n  - `resource.WithHost()` - hostname/IP\n  - `resource.WithProcessRuntime*()` - runtime details\n\n---\n\n## Deprecations\n\n### Jaeger Tracing Exporter\n\n> **Deprecated since:** v1.36.0\n> **Will be removed:** ~1 year from deprecation date\n\nThe Jaeger tracing exporter is deprecated. OpenTelemetry dropped support for direct Jaeger export in July 2023. Jaeger officially recommends using OTLP (OpenTelemetry Protocol).\n\n#### Migration Path\n\n**Before:**\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: jaeger\n  jaeger:\n    host: localhost\n    port: 6831\n```\n\n**After (using OTLP with Jaeger receiver):**\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: otlp\n  otlp:\n    endpoint: http://localhost:4317  # Jaeger OTLP gRPC receiver\n```\n\nFor Jaeger containers, use OpenTelemetry Collector or update your Jaeger deployment to use OTLP receivers.\n\n---\n\n### List Pagination: Offset Parameter\n\n> **Deprecated since:** v1.13.0\n> **Status:** Active (will be removed in a future release)\n\nThe `offset` parameter in list API calls is deprecated in favor of `page_token` for forward-compatible pagination.\n\n#### Affected API Methods\n- `ListFlagRequest`\n- `ListSegmentRequest`\n- `ListRuleRequest`\n- `ListNamespaceRequest`\n\n#### Migration Path\n\n**Before:**\n```bash\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/flags?limit=10&offset=20\n```\n\n**After:**\n```bash\n# First request\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/flags?limit=10\n\n# Response includes:\n# {\n#   \"flags\": [...],\n#   \"next_page_token\": \"eyJvZmZzZXQiOjEwfQ==\"\n# }\n\n# Next page request\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/flags?limit=10&page_token=eyJvZmZzZXQiOjEwfQ==\n```\n\n#### REST API Mapping (gRPC Gateway)\n```proto\n// Old way (deprecated)\nmessage ListFlagRequest {\n  int32 offset = 2 [deprecated = true];  // \u2190 Deprecated\n}\n\n// New way\nmessage ListFlagRequest {\n  string page_token = 3;  // \u2190 Use this instead\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## API Updates\n\n### EvaluationResponse Changes\n\nThe `EvaluationResponse` protobuf message includes the following structure:\n\n```proto\nmessage EvaluationResponse {\n  string request_id = 1;\n  string entity_id = 2;\n  map<string, string> request_context = 3;\n  bool match = 4;\n  string flag_key = 5;\n  string segment_key = 6 [deprecated = true];      // \u2190 Use segment_keys instead\n  google.protobuf.Timestamp timestamp = 7;\n  string value = 8;\n  double request_duration_millis = 9;\n  string attachment = 10;\n  EvaluationReason reason = 11;\n  string namespace_key = 12;\n  repeated string segment_keys = 13;               // \u2190 Multiple segments supported\n}\n```\n\n**Important:**\n- `segment_key` (singular) is deprecated. Use `segment_keys` (plural) which supports multiple segments\n- All segment keys are returned in the repeated `segment_keys` field\n\n### Flag Type Support\n\nThe API supports two flag types via the `FlagType` enum:\n\n```proto\nenum FlagType {\n  VARIANT_FLAG_TYPE = 0;   // Original flag type with variants\n  BOOLEAN_FLAG_TYPE = 1;   // Boolean true/false flags\n}\n```\n\nBoth types are fully supported in:\n- Flag evaluation (`Evaluate` and `BatchEvaluate`)\n- Flag management (CRUD operations)\n- Rules and rollouts\n- Segments and constraints\n\n---\n\n## Upgrade Guide\n\n### Prerequisites\n- Current Flipt version: v1.40.1 or later\n- Backup your database (recommended)\n- Note your current configuration for reference\n\n### Step 1: Update Flipt Binary\n\nDownload and install the latest Flipt release:\n\n```bash\n# macOS (Homebrew)\nbrew upgrade flipt\n\n# Linux (manual download)\nwget https://github.com/flipt-io/flipt/releases/download/vX.Y.Z/flipt_linux_amd64.tar.gz\ntar -xzf flipt_linux_amd64.tar.gz\nsudo mv flipt /usr/local/bin/\n```\n\n### Step 2: Review Configuration Changes (Optional)\n\nIf using tracing, you may want to add sampling configuration to reduce trace volume:\n\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  samplingRatio: 0.1  # Sample 10% of traces\n```\n\n### Step 3: (Optional) Enable Remote Configuration\n\nIf you want to store configuration in cloud storage:\n\n1. Upload your current `flipt.yml` to S3, Azure, or GCS\n2. Update `FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH` or configuration source to point to the remote URL\n3. Ensure service has appropriate cloud credentials\n\n### Step 4: Restart Flipt\n\n```bash\n# Stop the current instance\nsudo systemctl stop flipt\n\n# Start the new version\nsudo systemctl start flipt\n\n# Verify it's running\ncurl http://localhost:8080/health\n```\n\n### Step 5: Verify Functionality\n\nTest core features:\n\n```bash\n# Check server info\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/meta/info\n\n# List flags (using new pagination if needed)\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/flags?limit=10\n\n# Test evaluation\ncurl -X POST http://localhost:8080/api/v1/evaluate \\\n  -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \\\n  -d '{\n    \"flagKey\": \"my-flag\",\n    \"entityId\": \"user-123\"\n  }'\n```\n\n### Step 6: Monitor for Issues\n\nWatch logs and metrics for any issues:\n\n```bash\n# Check Flipt logs (adjust path based on your setup)\njournalctl -u flipt -f\n\n# Monitor metrics if using Prometheus\n# Check http://localhost:8080/metrics\n```\n\n### Rollback Plan\n\nIf you encounter issues:\n\n1. Stop the new Flipt version\n2. Restore the previous binary version\n3. Restart Flipt with the previous version\n4. Database is compatible, no migration needed\n\n---\n\n## Storage Backend Support\n\n### Database\n- SQLite (default)\n- PostgreSQL\n- MySQL\n- CockroachDB\n- LibSQL / Turso\n\n### Filesystem/Git\n- Local directory\n- Git repository (with polling)\n- S3\n- Azure Blob Storage\n- Google Cloud Storage\n- OCI (via registries)\n\n### Caching\n- In-memory (default)\n- Redis\n\n### Analytics\n- ClickHouse (with new entity ID tracking)\n\n---\n\n## Performance Recommendations\n\n1. **For Tracing:** Set `samplingRatio` to `0.1` or lower in production to reduce overhead\n2. **For Authentication:** Let Flipt optimize connections automatically; no configuration needed\n3. **For Remote Configuration:** Use regional cloud storage to reduce latency\n\n---\n\n## Support & Documentation\n\n- **Documentation:** https://flipt.io/docs\n- **GitHub Issues:** https://github.com/flipt-io/flipt/issues\n- **Discussions:** https://github.com/flipt-io/flipt/discussions\n\n---\n\n## Version Information\n\n- **Latest Release:** v1.40.1 (2024-04-11)\n- **Current Development:** After v1.40.1\n- **API Version:** v1 (REST), Protobuf (gRPC)\n- **Minimum Go Version:** 1.20+\n",

Restart Flipt\n\n---\n\n### Tracing: Sampling Ratio Configuration\n\n**Added in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)\n\nEnhanced OpenTelemetry tracing instrumentation with configurable trace sampling ratio. This allows you to control the percentage of requests that generate traces, reducing overhead in high-traffic environments.\n\n#### Configuration Schema\n\n**YAML Configuration:**\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: otlp\n  samplingRatio: 0.1  # Sample 10% of traces\n  otlp:\n    endpoint: http://localhost:4317\n```\n\n**Environment Variable:**\n```bash\nFLIPT_TRACING_SAMPLINGRATIO=0.1\n```\n\n#### Valid Values\n- Minimum: `0` (no traces sampled)\n- Maximum: `1` (all traces sampled, default)\n- Recommended for production: `0.1` to `0.5`\n\n#### Configuration Details\n- **Type:** Float64 (0.0 - 1.0)\n- **Default:** `1` (sample all traces)\n- **Validation:** Flipt validates that the value is between 0 and 1 at startup\n\n#### Implementation\n- Implemented using OpenTelemetry SDK's `TraceIDRatioBased` sampler\n- Applied at the TracerProvider level in `internal/tracing/tracing.go`\n- Sampler is initialized with: `tracesdk.TraceIDRatioBased(cfg.SamplingRatio)`\n\n#### API Example\nWhen creating a tracer provider programmatically:\n```go\ncfg := config.TracingConfig{\n    Enabled: true,\n    Exporter: config.TracingOTLP,\n    SamplingRatio: 0.1,\n}\nprovider, err := tracing.NewProvider(ctx, version, cfg)\n```\n\n#### Migration Path\n- This is a new optional feature; no migration required\n- Default behavior (sample all traces) unchanged unless explicitly configured\n- To reduce sampling:\n  1. Update your configuration file or environment variable\n  2. Set `samplingRatio` to desired value (e.g., `0.1` for 10%)\n  3. Restart Flipt\n\n---\n\n### Analytics: Entity ID Tracking\n\n**Added in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)\n\nEntity ID is now tracked in analytics data when using ClickHouse as the analytics backend. This enables better insights into which entities are being evaluated.\n\n#### Details\n- Entity ID values are now captured and stored in the analytics event stream\n- Tracked in addition to existing metrics (flag key, namespace, etc.)\n- Applies to ClickHouse analytics backend\n- Analytics can be queried to analyze entity usage patterns\n\n#### Configuration\nNo new configuration required. If you have ClickHouse analytics enabled, entity ID tracking is automatic:\n\n```yaml\nanalytics:\n  storage:\n    type: clickhouse\n    clickhouse:\n      endpoint: http://localhost:8123\n```\n\n---\n\n## Improvements\n\n### Authentication: Database Connection Optimization\n\n**Fixed in:** v1.40.1 (includes auth improvements)\n\nAuthentication backend now avoids establishing unnecessary database connections:\n- Connections are only established when authentication methods require them\n- Reduces database connection pool overhead\n- Improves startup time for authentication configurations that don't need a database\n\n#### Details\n- Applied in `internal/server/authn/` module\n- Only methods like token authentication that require database access will establish connections\n- Methods like OAuth/OIDC that don't need database remain lightweight\n\n---\n\n### Authentication: Cache Optimization\n\n**Fixed in:** v1.40.1\n\nAuthentication hash caching now stores only the hash rather than full authentication data:\n- Reduces cache memory usage\n- Improves cache performance\n- More secure (hashes instead of full auth data in cache)\n\n#### Implementation\n- Cache middleware in `internal/server/middleware/`\n- Only authentication hash is cached (`auth.Hash`)\n- Full authentication data still retrieved as needed\n\n---\n\n### OpenTelemetry Resource Attributes\n\n**Improved in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)\n\nOpenTelemetry tracing now includes enhanced resource information:\n- Service name: `flipt`\n- Service version: Current Flipt version\n- OTEL environment variables: Automatically detected from environment\n- Telemetry SDK information: Included in traces\n- Container information: Detected if running in container\n- Host information: System hostname/IP included\n- Process runtime details: Go version and runtime information\n\n#### Details\n- Implements OpenTelemetry semantic conventions v1.24.0\n- Applied when creating trace resource in `internal/tracing/tracing.go`\n- Configured in `newResource()` function with:\n  - `resource.WithFromEnv()` - picks up OTEL_* environment variables\n  - `resource.WithTelemetrySDK()` - includes SDK version\n  - `resource.WithContainer()` - container detection\n  - `resource.WithHost()` - hostname/IP\n  - `resource.WithProcessRuntime*()` - runtime details\n\n---\n\n## Deprecations\n\n### Jaeger Tracing Exporter\n\n> **Deprecated since:** v1.36.0\n> **Will be removed:** ~1 year from deprecation date\n\nThe Jaeger tracing exporter is deprecated. OpenTelemetry dropped support for direct Jaeger export in July 2023. Jaeger officially recommends using OTLP (OpenTelemetry Protocol).\n\n#### Migration Path\n\n**Before:**\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: jaeger\n  jaeger:\n    host: localhost\n    port: 6831\n```\n\n**After (using OTLP with Jaeger receiver):**\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: otlp\n  otlp:\n    endpoint: http://localhost:4317  # Jaeger OTLP gRPC receiver\n```\n\nFor Jaeger containers, use OpenTelemetry Collector or update your Jaeger deployment to use OTLP receivers.\n\n---\n\n### List Pagination: Offset Parameter\n\n> **Deprecated since:** v1.13.0\n> **Status:** Active (will be removed in a future release)\n\nThe `offset` parameter in list API calls is deprecated in favor of `page_token` for forward-compatible pagination.\n\n#### Affected API Methods\n- `ListFlagRequest`\n- `ListSegmentRequest`\n- `ListRuleRequest`\n- `ListNamespaceRequest`\n\n#### Migration Path\n\n**Before:**\n```bash\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/flags?limit=10&offset=20\n```\n\n**After:**\n```bash\n# First request\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/flags?limit=10\n\n# Response includes:\n# {\n#   \"flags\": [...],\n#   \"next_page_token\": \"eyJvZmZzZXQiOjEwfQ==\"\n# }\n\n# Next page request\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/flags?limit=10&page_token=eyJvZmZzZXQiOjEwfQ==\n```\n\n#### REST API Mapping (gRPC Gateway)\n```proto\n// Old way (deprecated)\nmessage ListFlagRequest {\n  int32 offset = 2 [deprecated = true];  // \u2190 Deprecated\n}\n\n// New way\nmessage ListFlagRequest {\n  string page_token = 3;  // \u2190 Use this instead\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## API Updates\n\n### EvaluationResponse Changes\n\nThe `EvaluationResponse` protobuf message includes the following structure:\n\n```proto\nmessage EvaluationResponse {\n  string request_id = 1;\n  string entity_id = 2;\n  map<string, string> request_context = 3;\n  bool match = 4;\n  string flag_key = 5;\n  string segment_key = 6 [deprecated = true];      // \u2190 Use segment_keys instead\n  google.protobuf.Timestamp timestamp = 7;\n  string value = 8;\n  double request_duration_millis = 9;\n  string attachment = 10;\n  EvaluationReason reason = 11;\n  string namespace_key = 12;\n  repeated string segment_keys = 13;               // \u2190 Multiple segments supported\n}\n```\n\n**Important:**\n- `segment_key` (singular) is deprecated. Use `segment_keys` (plural) which supports multiple segments\n- All segment keys are returned in the repeated `segment_keys` field\n\n### Flag Type Support\n\nThe API supports two flag types via the `FlagType` enum:\n\n```proto\nenum FlagType {\n  VARIANT_FLAG_TYPE = 0;   // Original flag type with variants\n  BOOLEAN_FLAG_TYPE = 1;   // Boolean true/false flags\n}\n```\n\nBoth types are fully supported in:\n- Flag evaluation (`Evaluate` and `BatchEvaluate`)\n- Flag management (CRUD operations)\n- Rules and rollouts\n- Segments and constraints\n\n---\n\n## Upgrade Guide\n\n### Prerequisites\n- Current Flipt version: v1.40.1 or later\n- Backup your database (recommended)\n- Note your current configuration for reference\n\n### Step 1: Update Flipt Binary\n\nDownload and install the latest Flipt release:\n\n```bash\n# macOS (Homebrew)\nbrew upgrade flipt\n\n# Linux (manual download)\nwget https://github.com/flipt-io/flipt/releases/download/vX.Y.Z/flipt_linux_amd64.tar.gz\ntar -xzf flipt_linux_amd64.tar.gz\nsudo mv flipt /usr/local/bin/\n```\n\n### Step 2: Review Configuration Changes (Optional)\n\nIf using tracing, you may want to add sampling configuration to reduce trace volume:\n\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  samplingRatio: 0.1  # Sample 10% of traces\n```\n\n### Step 3: (Optional) Enable Remote Configuration\n\nIf you want to store configuration in cloud storage:\n\n1. Upload your current `flipt.yml` to S3, Azure, or GCS\n2. Update `FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH` or configuration source to point to the remote URL\n3. Ensure service has appropriate cloud credentials\n\n### Step 4: Restart Flipt\n\n```bash\n# Stop the current instance\nsudo systemctl stop flipt\n\n# Start the new version\nsudo systemctl start flipt\n\n# Verify it's running\ncurl http://localhost:8080/health\n```\n\n### Step 5: Verify Functionality\n\nTest core features:\n\n```bash\n# Check server info\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/meta/info\n\n# List flags (using new pagination if needed)\ncurl http://localhost:8080/api/v1/flags?limit=10\n\n# Test evaluation\ncurl -X POST http://localhost:8080/api/v1/evaluate \\\n  -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \\\n  -d '{\n    \"flagKey\": \"my-flag\",\n    \"entityId\": \"user-123\"\n  }'\n```\n\n### Step 6: Monitor for Issues\n\nWatch logs and metrics for any issues:\n\n```bash\n# Check Flipt logs (adjust path based on your setup)\njournalctl -u flipt -f\n\n# Monitor metrics if using Prometheus\n# Check http://localhost:8080/metrics\n```\n\n### Rollback Plan\n\nIf you encounter issues:\n\n1. Stop the new Flipt version\n2. Restore the previous binary version\n3. Restart Flipt with the previous version\n4. Database is compatible, no migration needed\n\n---\n\n## Storage Backend Support\n\n### Database\n- SQLite (default)\n- PostgreSQL\n- MySQL\n- CockroachDB\n- LibSQL / Turso\n\n### Filesystem/Git\n- Local directory\n- Git repository (with polling)\n- S3\n- Azure Blob Storage\n- Google Cloud Storage\n- OCI (via registries)\n\n### Caching\n- In-memory (default)\n- Redis\n\n### Analytics\n- ClickHouse (with new entity ID tracking)\n\n---\n\n## Performance Recommendations\n\n1. **For Tracing:** Set `samplingRatio` to `0.1` or lower in production to reduce overhead\n2. **For Authentication:** Let Flipt optimize connections automatically; no configuration needed\n3. **For Remote Configuration:** Use regional cloud storage to reduce latency\n\n---\n\n## Support & Documentation\n\n- **Documentation:** https://flipt.io/docs\n- **GitHub Issues:** https://github.com/flipt-io/flipt/issues\n- **Discussions:** https://github.com/flipt-io/flipt/discussions\n\n---\n\n## Version Information\n\n- **Latest Release:** v1.40.1 (2024-04-11)\n- **Current Development:** After v1.40.1\n- **API Version:** v1 (REST), Protobuf (gRPC)\n- **Minimum Go Version:** 1.20+\n",

# Flipt Release Notes

## Overview

These release notes document the API and configuration changes in Flipt since v1.40.1, including new features, improvements, and important information for upgrading.

## Breaking Changes

No breaking changes identified in this release. All API changes are backward compatible.

## New Features

### Configuration: Remote Blob Storage Support

**Added in:** Unreleased (after v1.40.1)

Flipt now supports loading configuration files from remote blob storage backends. This enables storing your Flipt configuration in cloud object storage (S3, Azure Blob Storage, Google Cloud Storage) instead of local filesystem.

#### Supported Schemes
- **S3:** `s3://bucket-name/path/to/config.yml`
- **Azure Blob Storage:** `azblob://container/path/to/config.yml`
- **Google Cloud Storage:** `gs://bucket-name/path/to/config.yml`

#### Configuration Example
```bash
# Load configuration from S3
FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=s3://my-bucket/flipt-config.yml

# Load configuration from Azure Blob Storage
FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=azblob://mycontainer/flipt-config.yml

# Load configuration from Google Cloud Storage
FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH=gs://my-bucket/flipt-config.yml
```

#### API Details
- Configuration is loaded via the `getConfigFile()` function in `internal/config/config.go`
- The function supports URLs with schemes mapped to object storage backends
- Falls back to local filesystem if no recognized remote scheme is detected
- Requires appropriate cloud provider credentials/authentication configured in your environment

#### Migration Path
No migration needed. This is a new optional feature. You can continue using local configuration paths or migrate by:
1. Upload your current `flipt.yml` to your cloud storage
2. Set `FLIPT_CONFIG_PATH` environment variable to the remote URL
3. Restar
... (truncated)
